<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">1976 Summer Olympics</h1>

<p>The <b>1976 Summer Olympics</b>, officially called the <b>Games of the XXI Olympiad</b> (<a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: Les <i>XXIes olympiques d'été</i>), was an international <a href="/wiki/Multi-sport_event" title="Multi-sport event">multi-sport event</a> in <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a>, in 1976, and the first Olympic Games held in <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>. Montreal was awarded the rights to the 1976 Games on May 12, 1970, at the 69th <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IOC_Session" title="IOC Session">IOC Session</a> in <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>, over the bids of <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a> and <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>. It is so far the only Summer Olympic Games to be held in Canada. <a href="/wiki/Calgary" title="Calgary">Calgary</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vancouver" title="Vancouver">Vancouver</a> later hosted the Winter Olympic Games in <a href="/wiki/1988_Winter_Olympics" title="1988 Winter Olympics">1988</a> and <a href="/wiki/2010_Winter_Olympics" title="2010 Winter Olympics">2010</a>, respectively.</p>
<p>Twenty-nine countries, mostly African, boycotted the Montreal Games when the <a href="/wiki/International_Olympic_Committee" title="International Olympic Committee">International Olympic Committee</a> (IOC) refused to ban New Zealand, after the <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_national_rugby_union_team" title="New Zealand national rugby union team">New Zealand national rugby union team</a> had <a href="/wiki/1976_New_Zealand_rugby_union_tour_of_South_Africa" title="1976 New Zealand rugby union tour of South Africa">toured South Africa earlier in 1976</a> in defiance of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>' calls for a sporting embargo.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Host_city_selection">Host city selection</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1976_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Host city selection">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The vote occurred on May 12, 1970, at the 69th <a href="/wiki/List_of_IOC_meetings#IOC_Sessions" title="List of IOC meetings">IOC Session</a> in Amsterdam, <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>. While Los Angeles and Moscow were viewed as the favorites given that they represented the world's two main powers, many of the smaller countries supported Montreal as an <a href="/wiki/Underdog_(term)" title="Underdog (term)">underdog</a> and as a politically neutral site for the games. Los Angeles was eliminated after the first round and Montreal won in the second round. Moscow would go on to host the <a href="/wiki/1980_Summer_Olympics" title="1980 Summer Olympics">1980 Summer Olympics</a> and Los Angeles the <a href="/wiki/1984_Summer_Olympics" title="1984 Summer Olympics">1984 Summer Olympics</a>. One blank vote was cast in the second and final round.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-votes_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-votes-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a> had made its third attempt for the Olympics but failed to get the support of the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Olympic_Committee" title="Canadian Olympic Committee">Canadian Olympic Committee</a>, which selected Montreal instead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>

<p><a href="/wiki/Robert_Bourassa" title="Robert Bourassa">Robert Bourassa</a>, then the <a href="/wiki/Premier_of_Quebec" title="Premier of Quebec">Premier of Quebec</a>, first asked Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Trudeau" title="Pierre Trudeau">Pierre Trudeau</a> to advise <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Canada" title="Monarchy of Canada">Canada's monarch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a>, to attend the opening of the games. However, Bourassa later became unsettled about how unpopular the move might be with <a href="/wiki/Quebec_sovereignty_movement" title="Quebec sovereignty movement">sovereigntists in the province</a>, annoying Trudeau, who had already made arrangements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> The leader of the <a href="/wiki/Parti_Qu%C3%A9b%C3%A9cois" title="Parti Québécois">Parti Québécois</a> at the time, <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_L%C3%A9vesque" title="René Lévesque">René Lévesque</a>, sent his own letter to <a href="/wiki/Buckingham_Palace" title="Buckingham Palace">Buckingham Palace</a>, asking the Queen to refuse her prime minister's request, though she did not oblige Lévesque as he was out of his jurisdiction in offering advice to the Sovereign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cost_and_cost_overrun">Cost and cost overrun</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1976_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Cost and cost overrun">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <i>Oxford Olympics Study</i> estimates the outturn cost of the Montreal 1976 Summer Olympics at USD 6.1 billion in 2015-dollars and cost overrun at 720% in real terms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> This includes sports-related costs only, that is, (i) <i>operational costs</i> incurred by the organizing committee for the purpose of staging the Games, e.g., expenditures for technology, transportation, workforce, administration, security, catering, ceremonies, and medical services, and (ii) <i>direct capital costs</i> incurred by the host city and country or private investors to build, e.g., the competition venues, the Olympic village, international broadcast center, and media and press center, which are required to host the Games. Indirect capital costs are <i>not</i> included, such as for road, rail, or airport infrastructure, or for hotel upgrades or other business investment incurred in preparation for the Games but not directly related to staging the Games. The cost overrun for Montreal 1976 is the highest cost overrun on record for any Olympics. The cost and cost overrun for Montreal 1976 compares with costs of USD 4.6 billion and a cost overrun of 51% for Rio 2016 and USD 15 billion and 76% for London 2012. Average cost for the Summer Games since 1960 is USD 5.2 billion, average cost overrun is 176%.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Opening_ceremony">Opening ceremony</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1976_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Opening ceremony">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-style ambox-No_footnotes" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><img alt="" data-file-height="48" data-file-width="48" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg/40px-Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg/60px-Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg/80px-Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg.png 2x" width="40"/></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section includes a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">list of references</a>, related reading or <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:External_links" title="Wikipedia:External links">external links</a>, <b>but its sources remain unclear because it lacks <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#Inline_citations" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">inline citations</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help to <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Fact_and_Reference_Check" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Fact and Reference Check">improve</a> this section by <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:When_to_cite" title="Wikipedia:When to cite">introducing</a> more precise citations.</span> <small><i>(November 2012)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The opening ceremony of the 1976 Summer Olympic Games was held on Saturday, July 17, 1976, at the Olympic Stadium in <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a>, Quebec, in front of an audience of some 73,000 in the stadium, and an estimated half billion watching on television.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>The ceremony marked the opening of the Games of the XXI Olympiad, the first Olympics held in Canada (Calgary would later host the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1988_Olympic_Winter_Games" title="1988 Olympic Winter Games">1988 Olympic Winter Games</a>, and Vancouver the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2010_Olympic_Winter_Games" title="2010 Olympic Winter Games">2010 Olympic Winter Games</a>).</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R0716-0111,_Montreal,_XXI._Olympiade,_Cierpinski,_Reimann,_Stadtm%C3%BCller.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="603" data-file-width="800" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R0716-0111%2C_Montreal%2C_XXI._Olympiade%2C_Cierpinski%2C_Reimann%2C_Stadtm%C3%BCller.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R0716-0111%2C_Montreal%2C_XXI._Olympiade%2C_Cierpinski%2C_Reimann%2C_Stadtm%C3%BCller.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R0716-0111%2C_Montreal%2C_XXI._Olympiade%2C_Cierpinski%2C_Reimann%2C_Stadtm%C3%BCller.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R0716-0111%2C_Montreal%2C_XXI._Olympiade%2C_Cierpinski%2C_Reimann%2C_Stadtm%C3%BCller.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R0716-0111%2C_Montreal%2C_XXI._Olympiade%2C_Cierpinski%2C_Reimann%2C_Stadtm%C3%BCller.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R0716-0111%2C_Montreal%2C_XXI._Olympiade%2C_Cierpinski%2C_Reimann%2C_Stadtm%C3%BCller.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R0716-0111,_Montreal,_XXI._Olympiade,_Cierpinski,_Reimann,_Stadtm%C3%BCller.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
East German athletes Hans-Georg Reimann, Karl-Heinz Müller, and Waldemar Cierpinski at the Olympic Village</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Following an air show by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadian_Forces" title="Canadian Forces">Canadian Forces</a> <a href="/wiki/Royal_Canadian_Air_Force" title="Royal Canadian Air Force">Air Command</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Snowbirds" title="Snowbirds">Snowbirds</a> aerobatic flight demonstration squadron in the sunny skies above the stadium, the ceremony officially began at 3:00 pm with a trumpet fanfare and the arrival of <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a>, as Queen of Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> The Queen was accompanied by <a href="/wiki/Michael_Morris,_3rd_Baron_Killanin" title="Michael Morris, 3rd Baron Killanin">Michael Morris</a>, Lord Killanin, President of the International Olympic Committee, and was greeted to an orchestral rendition of ‘<a href="/wiki/O_Canada" title="O Canada">O Canada</a>’, an arrangement that for many years later would be used in schools across the country as well as in the daily sign off of CBC’s broadcast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>The queen entered the Royal Box with her consort, <a href="/wiki/Prince_Philip,_Duke_of_Edinburgh" title="Prince Philip, Duke of Edinburgh">Prince Philip, Duke of Edinburgh</a>, and her son, <a href="/wiki/Prince_Andrew,_Duke_of_York" title="Prince Andrew, Duke of York">Prince Andrew</a> (her daughter, <a href="/wiki/Anne,_Princess_Royal" title="Anne, Princess Royal">Princess Anne</a>, was an equestrian competitor for the team from Great Britain). She joined a number of Canadian and Olympic dignitaries, including: <a href="/wiki/Jules_L%C3%A9ger" title="Jules Léger">Jules Léger</a>, Governor General of Canada, and his wife, <a href="/wiki/Gabrielle_L%C3%A9ger" title="Gabrielle Léger">Gabrielle</a>; Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Trudeau" title="Pierre Trudeau">Pierre Trudeau</a> and wife, <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Trudeau" title="Margaret Trudeau">Margaret</a>; <a href="/wiki/Robert_Bourassa" title="Robert Bourassa">Robert Bourassa</a>, Premier of the Province of Quebec; <a href="/wiki/Roger_Rousseau" title="Roger Rousseau">Roger Rousseau</a>, chief of the Montreal Olympic Organizing Committee (COJO); Sheila Dunlop, Lady Killanin, wife of the IOC President; Mayor of Montreal, <a href="/wiki/Jean_Drapeau" title="Jean Drapeau">Jean Drapeau</a>, and his wife, Marie-Claire.</p>
<p>The parade of athletes began moments later with the arrival of the Greek team and concluded with the entrance of the Canadian team. All other teams entered the stadium according to French alphabetical order. Although most would eventually boycott the Games in the days to follow, a number of African delegations did march in the parade. Much of the music performed for the parade was arranged by <a href="/wiki/Vic_Vogel" title="Vic Vogel">Vic Vogel</a> and was inspired by late Quebec composer, <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Mathieu" title="André Mathieu">André Mathieu</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>Immediately following the parade, a troupe of 80 women dancers dressed in white (representing the 80th anniversary of the revival of the Olympic Games) performed a brief dance in the outline of the Olympic rings.</p>
<p>Following that came the official speeches, first by Roger Rousseau, head of the Montreal Olympic organizing committee, and Lord Killanin. Her Majesty was then invited to proclaim the Games open, which she did, first in French, then in English.</p>
<p>Accompanied by the Olympic Hymn, the Olympic flag was carried into the stadium and hoisted at the west end of the stadium. The flag was carried by eight men and hoisted by four women, representing the ten provinces and two territories (at the time) of Canada. As the flag was hoisted, an all-male choir performed an a cappella version of the Olympic Hymn.</p>
<p>Once the flag was unfurled, a troupe of Bavarian dancers, representing Munich, host of the previous <a href="/wiki/1972_Summer_Olympics" title="1972 Summer Olympics">1972 Summer Olympics</a>, entered the stadium with the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_symbols#Antwerp_flag" title="Olympic symbols">Antwerp Flag</a>. Following a brief dance, that flag was then passed from the Mayor of Munich to the IOC President and then to the Mayor of Montreal. Next came a presentation of traditional Québécois folk dancers. The two troupes merged in dance together to the strains of “Vive le Compagnie” and exited the stadium with the Antwerp Flag, which would be displayed at Montreal City Hall until the opening of the <a href="/wiki/1980_Summer_Olympics" title="1980 Summer Olympics">1980 Summer Olympics</a> in Moscow.</p>
<p>Three cannons were then fired, as the 80-member troupe of female dancers unfolded special crates that released doves and ribbons in the five Olympic colours.</p>
<p>Another trumpet fanfare announced the arrival of the Olympic Flame. The torch was carried by two 15-year-olds, Stéphane Préfontaine and Sandra Henderson, chosen as representatives of the unity within Canada’s linguistic heritage. This would also be the first time two people would light the Olympic flame, and Henderson would become only the second woman to do the honours. The duo would make a lap of the stadium and then climbed a staircase on a special dais at the center of the stadium to set the Olympic flame alight in a temporary white aluminum cauldron. The flame was later transported to a more permanent cauldron just outside the running track to burn throughout the duration of the Games. A choir then performed the Olympic Cantata as onlookers admired the Olympic flame.</p>
<p>Then, the ‘Youth of Canada’ took to the track to perform a colourful choreographed segment with flags, ribbons and a variety of rhythmic gymnast performers.</p>
<p>The flag bearers of each team then circled around the speaker’s dais as Pierre St-Jean recited the Athletes’ Oath and Maurice Forget recited the Judges’ Oath, in English and in French, with right hand over the heart and the Canadian flag clutched in the left.</p>
<p>Finally, a choral performance of ‘O Canada’ in both French and English marked the close of the opening ceremony, as the announcers concluded with a declaration of ‘Vive les Jeux de Montreal! Long Live the Montreal Games’.</p>
<p>The Montreal ceremony would be the last of its kind, as future Olympic ceremonies, beginning with the 1980 Moscow Games, would become more focused on theatrical, cultural and artistic presentations and less on formality and protocol.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Highlights">Highlights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1976_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Highlights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li>These Olympics were the first of two summer games to be organised under the IOC presidency of <a href="/wiki/Michael_Morris,_3rd_Baron_Killanin" title="Michael Morris, 3rd Baron Killanin">Michael Morris, 3rd Baron Killanin</a></li>
<li>At age 14, gymnast <a href="/wiki/Nadia_Com%C4%83neci" title="Nadia Comăneci">Nadia Comăneci</a> of Romania became the first person to score a <a href="/wiki/Perfect_10_(gymnastics)" title="Perfect 10 (gymnastics)">perfect 10</a> at the Olympics, recording seven 10.00 scores and winning three gold medals, including the <a href="/wiki/Gymnastics_at_the_1976_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_artistic_individual_all-around" title="Gymnastics at the 1976 Summer Olympics – Women's artistic individual all-around">All-Around</a>. The scoreboard could hold only 3 digits and the score was shown as 1.00. In women's gymnastics three gold medals were also won by <a href="/wiki/Nellie_Kim" title="Nellie Kim">Nellie Kim</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USSR_at_the_Summer_Olympics" title="USSR at the Summer Olympics">Soviet Union</a>. <a href="/wiki/Nikolai_Andrianov" title="Nikolai Andrianov">Nikolai Andrianov</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USSR" title="USSR">USSR</a> won four gold medals, including All Around, in men's gymnastics.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taro_Aso" title="Taro Aso">Taro Aso</a> was a member of the Japanese shooting team. 32 years later, he would be elected as the prime minister of Japan.</li>
<li>The Games were opened by <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a>, as <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Canada" title="Monarchy of Canada">head of state of Canada</a>, and several members of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Royal_Family" title="British Royal Family">Royal Family</a> attended the opening ceremonies. This was particularly significant, as these were the first Olympic games hosted on Canadian soil. The Queen's daughter, <a href="/wiki/Anne,_Princess_Royal" title="Anne, Princess Royal">Princess Anne</a>, also competed in the games as part of the British riding team.</li>
<li>After a rainstorm doused the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olympic_Flame" title="Olympic Flame">Olympic Flame</a> a few days after the games had opened, an official relit the flame using his cigarette lighter. Organizers quickly doused it again and relit it using a backup of the original flame.</li>
<li>The Israeli team walked into the stadium at the opening ceremony wearing black ribbons in commemoration of the 1972 <a href="/wiki/Munich_massacre" title="Munich massacre">Munich massacre</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></li>
<li>Women's events were introduced in basketball, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Team_handball" title="Team handball">handball</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rowing_(sport)" title="Rowing (sport)">rowing</a>.</li>
<li>Canada, the host country, finished with five silver and six bronze medals. This was the first time that the host country of the Summer Games had not won any <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gold_medals" title="Gold medals">gold medals</a>. This feat had occurred previously only in the Winter Games – <a href="/wiki/1924_Winter_Olympics" title="1924 Winter Olympics">1924</a> in <a href="/wiki/Chamonix" title="Chamonix">Chamonix</a>, France and <a href="/wiki/1928_Winter_Olympics" title="1928 Winter Olympics">1928</a> in <a href="/wiki/St._Moritz" title="St. Moritz">St. Moritz</a>, Switzerland. This later occurred at the <a href="/wiki/1984_Winter_Olympics" title="1984 Winter Olympics">1984 Winter Games</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sarajevo" title="Sarajevo">Sarajevo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a>, and again at the <a href="/wiki/1988_Winter_Olympics" title="1988 Winter Olympics">1988 Winter Olympics</a> in <a href="/wiki/Calgary" title="Calgary">Calgary</a>, Alberta, Canada.</li>
<li>Because of the <a href="/wiki/Munich_massacre" title="Munich massacre">Munich massacre</a>, security at these games was visible, as it had been earlier in the year at the <a href="/wiki/1976_Winter_Olympics" title="1976 Winter Olympics">Winter games</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Innsbruck,_Austria" title="Innsbruck, Austria">Innsbruck, Austria</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Viktor_Saneyev" title="Viktor Saneyev">Viktor Saneyev</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> won his third consecutive <a href="/wiki/Triple_jump" title="Triple jump">triple jump</a> gold medal, while <a href="/wiki/Klaus_Dibiasi" title="Klaus Dibiasi">Klaus Dibiasi</a> of Italy did the same in the platform <a href="/wiki/Diving" title="Diving">diving</a> event.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alberto_Juantorena" title="Alberto Juantorena">Alberto Juantorena</a> of Cuba became the first man to win both the 400 m and 800 m at the same Olympics.</li>
<li>Finland's <a href="/wiki/Lasse_Vir%C3%A9n" title="Lasse Virén">Lasse Virén</a> repeated his <a href="/wiki/1972_Summer_Olympics" title="1972 Summer Olympics">1972</a> double win in the 5,000 and 10,000 m runs, the first runner to successfully defend a 5,000 m win (since equalled by Britain's Mo Farah in 2016). Virén finished 5th in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marathon_(sport)" title="Marathon (sport)">marathon</a>, thereby failing to equal <a href="/wiki/Emil_Z%C3%A1topek" title="Emil Zátopek">Emil Zátopek</a>'s 1952 achievements.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hasely_Crawford" title="Hasely Crawford">Hasely Crawford</a> won Trinidad and Tobago's first Olympic gold medal by finishing first in the 100 meter dash.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Boris_Onishchenko" title="Boris Onishchenko">Boris Onishchenko</a>, a member of the Soviet Union's <a href="/wiki/Modern_pentathlon" title="Modern pentathlon">modern pentathlon</a> team, was disqualified after it was discovered that he had rigged his <a href="/wiki/%C3%89p%C3%A9e" title="Épée">épée</a> to register a hit when there wasn't one. Because of this, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USSR" title="USSR">USSR</a> modern pentathlon team was disqualified. Onischenko earned the enmity of other Soviet Olympic team members: for example, USSR volleyball team members threatened to throw him out of the hotel's window if they met him. Due to his disqualification, it was suggested that he earned the nickname of "Boris DISonish-chenko".</li>
<li>Five American <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxers</a> – <a href="/wiki/Sugar_Ray_Leonard" title="Sugar Ray Leonard">Sugar Ray Leonard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leon_Spinks" title="Leon Spinks">Leon Spinks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Spinks" title="Michael Spinks">Michael Spinks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leo_Randolph" title="Leo Randolph">Leo Randolph</a> and <a href="/wiki/Howard_Davis_Jr." title="Howard Davis Jr.">Howard Davis Jr.</a> won gold medals in <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxing</a>. This has been often called the greatest Olympic boxing team the United States ever had, and, out of the five American gold medalists in boxing, all but Davis went on to become professional world champions.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Anne,_Princess_Royal" title="Anne, Princess Royal">Princess Anne</a> of the United Kingdom was the only female competitor not to have to submit to a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sex_determination_in_sports" title="Sex determination in sports">sex test</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> She was a member of her country's <a href="/wiki/Equestrianism" title="Equestrianism">equestrian</a> team.</li>
<li>Japanese gymnast <a href="/wiki/Shun_Fujimoto" title="Shun Fujimoto">Shun Fujimoto</a> performed on a broken right knee, and helped the Japanese team win the gold medal for the team <a href="/wiki/Gymnastics_at_the_1976_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_artistic_team_all-around" title="Gymnastics at the 1976 Summer Olympics – Men's artistic team all-around">championship</a>. Fujimoto broke his leg on the floor exercise, and due to the closeness in the overall standings with the USSR, he hid the extent of the injury. With a broken knee, Fujimoto was able to complete his event on the rings, performing a perfect triple somersault dismount, maintaining perfect posture. He scored a 9.7 thus securing gold for Japan. Years later, when asked if he would do it again, he stated bluntly "No, I would not."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/East_German" title="East German">East German</a> women's swimming team won all but two gold medals. <a href="/wiki/Kornelia_Ender" title="Kornelia Ender">Kornelia Ender</a> won four gold medals and a silver medal.</li>
<li>The U.S. men's swimming team won all but one gold medal. <a href="/wiki/John_Naber" title="John Naber">John Naber</a> won four gold medals and a silver medal.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Luann_Ryon" title="Luann Ryon">Luann Ryon</a> won the women's <a href="/wiki/Archery" title="Archery">Archery</a> gold for the USA; Ryon had never before competed at the international level.</li>
<li>U.S. track and field athlete <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bruce_Jenner" title="Bruce Jenner">Bruce Jenner</a> won the gold medal for <a href="/wiki/Decathlon" title="Decathlon">decathlon</a>, setting a world record of 8,634 points.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alex_Oakley" title="Alex Oakley">Alex Oakley</a>, the Canadian race walker, became the oldest track and field athlete to compete at the Olympic Games. He was aged 50, and taking part in his fifth Olympics.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_men%27s_national_field_hockey_team" title="New Zealand men's national field hockey team">New Zealand men's national field hockey team</a> beat Australia to win gold, becoming the first non-Asian/European team to win the gold medal in hockey. It is also the first Olympic games in which hockey was played on artificial turf.</li>
<li>The Polish men's volleyball team came back from being down 2 sets against the USSR to win the gold medal.</li>
<li>Twenty-year-old <a href="/wiki/Morehouse_College" title="Morehouse College">Morehouse College</a> student <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Moses" title="Edwin Moses">Edwin Moses</a> sets a new world record in the 400m hurdles, less than a year after taking up the event. He is also America's only male individual track gold medalist.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Thomas_Bach" title="Thomas Bach">Thomas Bach</a> of <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West Germany</a> won a gold medal in the <a href="/wiki/Fencing_at_the_1976_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_team_foil" title="Fencing at the 1976 Summer Olympics – Men's team foil">team foil</a> event in <a href="/wiki/Fencing_at_the_1976_Summer_Olympics" title="Fencing at the 1976 Summer Olympics">fencing</a>. He would later become <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IOC_President" title="IOC President">IOC President</a>.</li>
<li>Heavyweight boxer <a href="/wiki/Clarence_Hill_(boxer)" title="Clarence Hill (boxer)">Clarence Hill</a> won a bronze medal for <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a>. His accomplishment makes Bermuda the smallest nation in terms of population to win an Olympic medal at the Summer Olympics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Venues">Venues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1976_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Venues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Montreal_Olympic_Park">Montreal Olympic Park</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1976_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Montreal Olympic Park">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Park,_Montreal" title="Olympic Park, Montreal">Olympic Park, Montreal</a></div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Olympic_Stadium_(Montreal)" title="Olympic Stadium (Montreal)">Olympic Stadium</a> – Opening/Closing ceremonies, Athletics, Football (final), Equestrian (jumping team final)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olympic_Pool_(Montreal)" title="Olympic Pool (Montreal)">Olympic Pool</a> – Diving, Modern pentathlon (swimming), Swimming, Water polo (final)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Montreal_Biodome" title="Montreal Biodome">Olympic Velodrome</a> – Cycling (track), Judo</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Montreal_Botanical_Garden" title="Montreal Botanical Garden">Montreal Botanical Garden</a> – Athletics (20 km walk), Modern pentathlon (running)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Maurice_Richard_Arena" title="Maurice Richard Arena">Maurice Richard Arena</a> – Boxing, Wrestling (freestyle finals)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Centre_Pierre_Charbonneau" title="Centre Pierre Charbonneau">Centre Pierre Charbonneau</a> – Wrestling</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Olympic_Village_(Montreal)" title="Olympic Village (Montreal)">Olympic Village</a> – Athletes' residence</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Venues_in_Greater_Montreal">Venues in Greater Montreal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1976_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Venues in Greater Montreal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C3%8Ele_Notre-Dame" title="Île Notre-Dame">Olympic Basin, Île Notre-Dame</a> – Canoeing, Rowing</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Complexe_sportif_Claude-Robillard" title="Complexe sportif Claude-Robillard">Claude Robillard Centre</a> – Handball, Water polo</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Centre_%C3%89tienne_Desmarteau" title="Centre Étienne Desmarteau">Centre Étienne Desmarteau</a> – Basketball</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/St._Michel_Arena" title="St. Michel Arena">St. Michel Arena</a> – Weightlifting</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paul_Sauv%C3%A9_Centre" title="Paul Sauvé Centre">Paul Sauvé Centre</a> – Volleyball</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Montreal_Forum" title="Montreal Forum">Montreal Forum</a> – Basketball (finals), Boxing (finals), Gymnastics, Handball (finals), Volleyball (finals)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mount_Royal" title="Mount Royal">Mount Royal Park</a> – Cycling (individual road race)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Quebec_Autoroute_40" title="Quebec Autoroute 40">Quebec Autoroute 40</a> – Cycling (road team time trial)</li>
<li>Streets of Montreal – Athletics (marathon)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Winter_Stadium_(Montreal)" title="Winter Stadium (Montreal)">Winter Stadium, Université de Montréal</a> – Fencing, Modern pentathlon (fencing)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Percival_Molson_Memorial_Stadium" title="Percival Molson Memorial Stadium">Molson Stadium, McGill University</a> – Field hockey</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Venues_outside_Montreal">Venues outside Montreal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1976_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Venues outside Montreal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<li><a href="/wiki/PEPS" title="PEPS">Pavilion de l'éducation physique et des sports de l'Université Laval</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quebec_City" title="Quebec City">Quebec City</a>, Quebec – Handball preliminaries</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Municipal_Stadium_(Sherbrooke)" title="Municipal Stadium (Sherbrooke)">Sherbrooke Stadium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sherbrooke" title="Sherbrooke">Sherbrooke</a>, Quebec – Football preliminaries</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palais_des_Sports_(Sherbrooke)" title="Palais des Sports (Sherbrooke)">Sherbrooke Sports Palace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sherbrooke" title="Sherbrooke">Sherbrooke</a>, Quebec – Handball preliminaries</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Olympic_Harbour" title="Portsmouth Olympic Harbour">Portsmouth Olympic Harbour</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingston,_Ontario" title="Kingston, Ontario">Kingston, Ontario</a> – Sailing</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Varsity_Stadium" title="Varsity Stadium">Varsity Stadium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>, Ontario – Football preliminaries</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frank_Clair_Stadium" title="Frank Clair Stadium">Lansdowne Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ottawa" title="Ottawa">Ottawa</a>, Ontario – Football preliminaries</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1976_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MontrealOlympicTowerAndBiodome1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="800" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/MontrealOlympicTowerAndBiodome1.jpg/300px-MontrealOlympicTowerAndBiodome1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/MontrealOlympicTowerAndBiodome1.jpg/450px-MontrealOlympicTowerAndBiodome1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/MontrealOlympicTowerAndBiodome1.jpg/600px-MontrealOlympicTowerAndBiodome1.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MontrealOlympicTowerAndBiodome1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Velodrome (foreground) and Olympic Stadium (its tower completed after the Games), Montreal</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There was a desire by the IOC's program commission to reduce the number of competitors and a number of recommendations were put to the IOC's executive board on 23 February 1973, which were all accepted. Rowing was the only sport where the number of competitors was increased, and women were admitted for the first time in Olympic history. The 1976 Summer Olympic programme featured 196 events with 198 medal ceremonies in the following 21 sports:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOfficial_Report_of_the_Organising_Committee1978116_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOfficial_Report_of_the_Organising_Committee1978116-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2;">
<ul>
<li>Aquatics
<ul>
<li><img alt="" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Diving_pictogram.svg/20px-Diving_pictogram.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Diving_pictogram.svg/30px-Diving_pictogram.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Diving_pictogram.svg/40px-Diving_pictogram.svg.png 2x" width="20"/> <a href="/wiki/Diving_at_the_1976_Summer_Olympics" title="Diving at the 1976 Summer Olympics">Diving</a> <small>(4)</small></li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Medal_count">Medal count</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1976_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Medal count">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>These are the top ten nations that won medals at the 1976 Games. Canada placed 27th with only 11 medals in total — none of them being gold. Canada remains the only host nation of a Summer Olympics that did not win at least one gold medal in its own games. It also did not win any gold medals at the <a href="/wiki/1988_Winter_Olympics" title="1988 Winter Olympics">1988 Winter Olympics</a> in <a href="/wiki/Calgary" title="Calgary">Calgary</a>. However, Canada went on to win the most gold medals at the <a href="/wiki/2010_Winter_Olympics" title="2010 Winter Olympics">2010 Winter Olympics</a> in <a href="/wiki/Vancouver" title="Vancouver">Vancouver</a>.</p>
<p>East Germany surpassed all expectations for a middle-sized nation by finishing 2nd. However, the GDR’s achievements were later fundamentally undermined by the expose of a serious and systematic scheme of doping by the East German sporting authorities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> It was later revealed that after injecting athletes with performance-boosting drugs at the Montreal Olympics, East German officials dumped the leftover serum and syringes in the <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lawrence_River" title="Saint Lawrence River">Saint Lawrence River</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Participating_National_Olympic_Committees">Participating National Olympic Committees</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1976_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Participating National Olympic Committees">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1976_Summer_Olympic_games_countries.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="628" data-file-width="1357" height="102" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/1976_Summer_Olympic_games_countries.png/220px-1976_Summer_Olympic_games_countries.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/1976_Summer_Olympic_games_countries.png/330px-1976_Summer_Olympic_games_countries.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/1976_Summer_Olympic_games_countries.png/440px-1976_Summer_Olympic_games_countries.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1976_Summer_Olympic_games_countries.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Participating nations</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1976_Summer_olympics_team_numbers.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="628" data-file-width="1357" height="102" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/1976_Summer_olympics_team_numbers.gif/220px-1976_Summer_olympics_team_numbers.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/1976_Summer_olympics_team_numbers.gif/330px-1976_Summer_olympics_team_numbers.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/1976_Summer_olympics_team_numbers.gif/440px-1976_Summer_olympics_team_numbers.gif 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1976_Summer_olympics_team_numbers.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Number of athletes</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Four nations made their first Summer Olympic appearance in Montreal: Andorra (which had its overall Olympic debut a few months before in <a href="/wiki/1976_Winter_Olympics" title="1976 Winter Olympics">Innsbruck Winter Olympics</a>), Antigua and Barbuda (as <i>Antigua</i>), <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Islands" title="Cayman Islands">Cayman Islands</a>, and Papua New Guinea.</p>
<p>Numbers in parentheses indicate the number of athletes from each nation that competed at the Games.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Non-participating_National_Olympic_Committees"><span id="Boycott"></span>Non-participating National Olympic Committees</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1976_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Non-participating National Olympic Committees">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Twenty-nine countries boycotted the Games<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-or_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-or-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-21">[21]</a></sup> due to the refusal of the IOC to ban New Zealand, after the <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_national_rugby_union_team" title="New Zealand national rugby union team">New Zealand national rugby union team</a> had <a href="/wiki/1976_New_Zealand_rugby_union_tour_of_South_Africa" title="1976 New Zealand rugby union tour of South Africa">toured South Africa earlier in 1976</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> The boycott was led by Congolese official <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jean_Claude_Ganga&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jean Claude Ganga (page does not exist)">Jean Claude Ganga</a>. Some of the boycotting nations (including Morocco, Cameroon and Egypt) had already participated, however, and withdrew after the first few days. <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast" title="Ivory Coast">Ivory Coast</a> were the only African countries that competed throughout the duration of the Games. Elsewhere, both Iraq and Guyana also opted to join the Congolese-led boycott. South Africa had been banned from the Olympics since 1964 due to its <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">apartheid</a> policies. Other countries, such as El Salvador and Zaire, did not participate in Montreal because of economic reasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-or_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-or-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:372px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1976_Summer_Olympics_(Montr%C3%A9al)_boycotting_countries_blue.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="625" data-file-width="1425" height="162" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/1976_Summer_Olympics_%28Montr%C3%A9al%29_boycotting_countries_blue.png/370px-1976_Summer_Olympics_%28Montr%C3%A9al%29_boycotting_countries_blue.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/1976_Summer_Olympics_%28Montr%C3%A9al%29_boycotting_countries_blue.png/555px-1976_Summer_Olympics_%28Montr%C3%A9al%29_boycotting_countries_blue.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/1976_Summer_Olympics_%28Montr%C3%A9al%29_boycotting_countries_blue.png/740px-1976_Summer_Olympics_%28Montr%C3%A9al%29_boycotting_countries_blue.png 2x" width="370"/></a>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Republic_of_China_boycott">Republic of China boycott</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1976_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Republic of China boycott">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>An unrelated boycott of the Montreal Games was the name issue between the Republic of China (ROC) and the People’s Republic of China (PRC). The ROC team withdrew from the games when Canada's <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_of_Canada" title="Liberal Party of Canada">Liberal</a> government under <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Trudeau" title="Pierre Trudeau">Pierre Trudeau</a> told it that the name "Republic of China" was not permissible at the Games because Canada had officially recognized the PRC in 1970. Canada attempted a compromise by allowing the ROC the continued use of its national flag and anthem in the Montreal Olympic activities; the ROC refused. Later in November 1976, the IOC recognized the PRC as the only recognized name of any Olympic activities representative of any Chinese government. In 1979 the IOC established in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nagoya_Resolution" title="Nagoya Resolution">Nagoya Resolution</a> that the PRC agreed to participate in IOC activities if the Republic of China was referred to as "<a href="/wiki/Chinese_Taipei" title="Chinese Taipei">Chinese Taipei</a>". <a href="/wiki/1980_Summer_Olympics" title="1980 Summer Olympics">Another boycott</a> would occur before the ROC would accept the provisions of the 1979 Resolution although the reason that so many other countries boycotted were not all the <a href="/wiki/1980_Summer_Olympics_boycott" title="1980 Summer Olympics boycott">same as the ROC</a>.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1976_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The legacy of the Montreal Olympics is complex. Many citizens regard the Olympiad as a financial disaster for the city as it faced debts for 30 years after the Games had finished. The retractable roof of the Olympic Stadium never properly worked and on several occasions has torn, prompting the stadium to be closed for extended periods of time for repairs. The failure of the <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Expos" title="Montreal Expos">Montreal Expos</a> baseball club is largely blamed on the failure of the Olympic Stadium to transition into an effective and popular venue for the club - given the massive capacity of the stadium, it often looked unimpressive even with regular crowds in excess of 20,000 spectators.</p>
<p>The year 1976 was also when the <a href="/wiki/Parti_Qu%C3%A9b%C3%A9cois" title="Parti Québécois">Parti Québécois</a> was first elected in Quebec, leading to new legislation to strengthen the legal status of the province's French-speaking majority; this also had the effect of driving migration of English speakers out of the province, especially to Ontario, whose capital city, Toronto, gained greater economic prominence as a result.</p>
<p>Montreal’s economy was also changing much like other industrial cities in the Great Lakes and Saint Lawrence River region of North America. In sum, numerous political, socio-cultural and economic changes affected the city at around the same time as the Olympics that would result in stalled growth and give the appearance of decline. That said, many of these factors existed prior to the Olympics and continued to have an effect on Montreal’s growth and relative importance many years afterwards. It’s not definitively proven that the Montreal Olympics played a specific role in that decline.</p>
<p>The relative benefits of the Olympics were defined differently to the Olympics of the 21st century, as was the method they were financed and presented to the public.</p>
<p>The Quebec provincial government took over construction when it became evident in 1975 that work had fallen far behind schedule. Work was still ongoing just weeks before the opening date, and the tower was not built. Mayor <a href="/wiki/Jean_Drapeau" title="Jean Drapeau">Jean Drapeau</a> had confidently predicted in 1970 that “the Olympics can no more have a deficit than a man can have a baby”, but the debt racked up to a billion dollars that the Quebec government mandated the city pay in full. This would prompt cartoonist <a href="/wiki/Terry_Mosher" title="Terry Mosher">Aislin</a> to draw a pregnant Drapeau on the telephone saying, "Allo, <a href="/wiki/Henry_Morgentaler" title="Henry Morgentaler">Morgentaler</a>?" in reference to a Montreal abortion provider.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:OlympicStadium.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1448" data-file-width="3008" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/OlympicStadium.jpg/300px-OlympicStadium.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/OlympicStadium.jpg/450px-OlympicStadium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/OlympicStadium.jpg/600px-OlympicStadium.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:OlympicStadium.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Olympic Stadium, seen next to the <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Botanical_Garden" title="Montreal Botanical Garden">Montreal Botanical Garden</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Olympic_Stadium_(Montreal)" title="Olympic Stadium (Montreal)">The Olympic Stadium</a> was designed by French architect <a href="/wiki/Roger_Taillibert" title="Roger Taillibert">Roger Taillibert</a>. It is often nicknamed “The Big O” as a reference to both its name and to the doughnut-shape of the permanent component of the stadium’s roof, though “The Big Owe” has been used to reference the astronomical cost of the stadium and the 1976 Olympics as a whole. It has never had an effective retractable roof, and the tower (called the Montreal Tower) was completed only after the Olympic Games were over. In December 2006 the stadium’s costs were finally paid in full.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> The total expenditure (including repairs, renovations, construction, <a href="/wiki/Interest" title="Interest">interest</a>, and inflation) amounted to C$1.61 billion. Today the stadium lacks a permanent tenant, as the <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Alouettes" title="Montreal Alouettes">Montreal Alouettes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Expos" title="Montreal Expos">Montreal Expos</a> have moved, though it does host some individual games of the Alouettes as well as the <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Impact" title="Montreal Impact">Montreal Impact</a>.</p>
<p>One of the streets surrounding the Olympic Stadium was renamed to honor <a href="/wiki/Pierre_de_Coubertin" title="Pierre de Coubertin">Pierre de Coubertin</a>, the founder of the Olympics.</p>
<p>The boycott by African nations over the inclusion of New Zealand, whose rugby team had played in South Africa that year, was a contributing factor in the massive protests and civil disobedience that occurred during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1981_Springbok_Tour" title="1981 Springbok Tour">1981 Springbok Tour</a> of New Zealand. Official sporting contacts between South Africa and New Zealand did not occur again until after the fall of apartheid.</p>
<p>Australia’s failure to win a gold medal led the country to create the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Institute_of_Sport" title="Australian Institute of Sport">Australian Institute of Sport</a>.</p>
<p>In 2016, the 40th Anniversary Celebrations were held. In conjunction with the celebrations, the 2016 <a href="/wiki/Quebec_Games" title="Quebec Games">Quebec Games</a> were held.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Global-2016-07-12_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-Global-2016-07-12-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
